skill_id: "27-accessorials-tracking"
name: "Accessorials Tracking"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 14
priority: high
trigger: "Activated at load booking. Runs through delivery and invoicing to ensure every accessorial is claimed."
inputs:
  - load_id: "string"
  - rc_accessorials: "all accessorials locked in rate confirmation"
  - detention_data: "from 16-detention-layover-management"
  - lumper_receipts: "from driver"
  - extra_stop_data: "timestamps and confirmation"
outputs:
  - accessorials_claim_summary: "total of all billable extras"
  - invoice_line_items: "formatted for invoicing skill"
  - missing_documentation: "any claims lacking proof"
integrations:
  - TMS
  - WhatsApp/SMS (driver document requests)
  - 16-detention-layover-management
  - 17-pod-invoicing-factoring
depends_on: ["12-rate-confirmation-review", "16-detention-layover-management"]
triggers_next: ["17-pod-invoicing-factoring"]
tags: [accessorials, detention, lumper, tonu, extra-stops, claims, billing]
---

# SKILL: Accessorials Tracking
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: Activated at booking. Runs through full invoice cycle.
**Phase**: 14 (concurrent with transit + detention)
**Priority**: HIGH

---

## Purpose

Every dollar of accessorial revenue must be captured, documented, and invoiced. Industry data shows dispatchers miss 15–25% of accessorial claims due to poor tracking. This skill ensures nothing is left on the table.

---

## Accessorial Types Reference

| Accessorial | When Applies | Typical Rate | Documentation Needed |
|-------------|-------------|-------------|---------------------|
| Detention — Pickup | Dwell >2 hrs at shipper | $25–75/hr | Arrival/departure timestamps, BOL times |
| Detention — Delivery | Dwell >2 hrs at receiver | $25–75/hr | Arrival/departure timestamps, BOL times |
| Layover | Driver holds overnight | $150–400/night | Timestamps, location proof |
| TONU | Load cancelled after dispatch | $150–300 flat | Dispatch confirmation, cancellation notice |
| Extra Stop | More than 1 pickup or delivery | $50–150/stop | Signed stop BOL, address |
| Driver Assist | Driver helps load/unload | $50–150 flat | RC clause, driver confirmation |
| Lumper | Third-party unloaders | Actual cost | Lumper receipt |
| Fuel Surcharge | If separate from rate | Varies | Per RC terms |
| NYC Surcharge | Delivery in NYC metro | $150–300 flat | If agreed in RC |
| Overweight | Load exceeds standard weight | $100–300 | Weight ticket |
| Reefer Breakdown | Reefer unit fails on temp load | Varies | Maintenance record, temp logs |
| Truck Ordered Not Used (TONU) | Load cancelled | $150–300 | Per RC |

---

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — RC Accessorial Extraction (At Booking)

Parse signed Rate Confirmation to extract all agreed accessorials:

```json
{
  "load_id": "TMS-2026-0392",
  "rc_accessorials": {
    "detention": {
      "free_hours": 2,
      "rate_per_hour": 50,
      "applies_to": ["pickup", "delivery"]
    },
    "tonu": {
      "amount": 150,
      "trigger": "cancelled_after_dispatch"
    },
    "driver_assist": {
      "amount": 75,
      "confirmed": false
    },
    "lumper": {
      "payer": "broker",
      "auth_process": "call_broker_for_code"
    },
    "extra_stops": null,
    "nyc_surcharge": null
  }
}
```

Create accessorial checklist in TMS. Every item on this list must be monitored and claimed if triggered.

### Step 2 — Live Tracking During Transit

Monitor each accessorial trigger in real time:

**Detention triggers:**
- Geo-fence arrival → start detention clock (handled by skill 16)
- Receive timestamps from skill 16 every hour
- Update TMS running total

**Lumper triggers:**
- Driver messages "lumper at receiver" → immediately:
  1. Request lumper receipt amount
  2. If broker-paid: call broker for auth code before lumper starts
  3. If carrier-paid: instruct driver to get receipt with amount + company name

**Extra stop triggers:**
- GPS confirms truck at additional address not on original RC
- Request driver confirmation and stop BOL
- Log extra stop in TMS

**Driver assist triggers:**
- Driver messages "had to help unload" → log immediately with timestamp
- Request confirmation message from broker that assist was required

**TONU triggers:**
- Broker calls/emails to cancel load
- Immediately log: TONU_TRIGGERED, timestamp, driver location
- Confirm TONU amount per RC

### Step 3 — Documentation Collection

For each triggered accessorial, collect proof:

| Accessorial | Required Proof |
|-------------|---------------|
| Detention | Geo-fence timestamps + BOL in/out times |
| Lumper | Signed lumper receipt with amount, date, company |
| Extra stop | Signed stop BOL from additional location |
| Driver assist | Broker email/message confirming or RC clause |
| TONU | Broker cancellation message/email + driver location proof |
| Layover | Timestamped driver log + location proof |
| Overweight | Weight ticket from certified scale |

If documentation is missing, request immediately:
> "Driver — I need the lumper receipt photo RIGHT NOW to bill it back. Send me a clear photo of the receipt showing the amount and company name."

### Step 4 — Claim Calculation

After delivery (before invoice generation):

```python
total_accessorials = 0

# Detention
if detention_pickup.billable_hours > 0:
    detention_pu_amount = detention_pickup.billable_hours × rc.detention_rate
    total_accessorials += detention_pu_amount
    
if detention_delivery.billable_hours > 0:
    detention_del_amount = detention_delivery.billable_hours × rc.detention_rate
    total_accessorials += detention_del_amount

# Lumper
if lumper_receipt_received:
    lumper_amount = parse_receipt(lumper_receipt)
    if rc.lumper_payer == "broker":
        total_accessorials += lumper_amount
    # If carrier-paid: it's already accounted for as carrier cost

# TONU
if tonu_triggered:
    total_accessorials += rc.tonu_amount

# Extra stops
for stop in extra_stops:
    if stop.confirmed and rc.extra_stop_rate:
        total_accessorials += rc.extra_stop_rate

# Driver assist
if driver_assist_confirmed:
    total_accessorials += rc.driver_assist_amount

# Layover
if layover_triggered:
    total_accessorials += rc.layover_rate × layover_nights
```

### Step 5 — Pre-Invoice Verification

Before submitting to invoicing skill:
- [ ] All triggered accessorials have documentation
- [ ] All amounts match RC terms exactly
- [ ] No undocumented claims included
- [ ] TONU documented with broker cancellation proof
- [ ] Lumper receipt is legible and shows correct amount

Flag any claim without full documentation as `NEEDS_DOCUMENTATION` — do not invoice undocumented claims.

### Step 6 — Pass to Invoicing

Send complete accessorial package to `17-pod-invoicing-factoring`:

```json
{
  "load_id": "TMS-2026-0392",
  "linehaul_rate": 700.00,
  "accessorials": [
    {
      "type": "detention_pickup",
      "hours": 1.25,
      "rate": 50,
      "amount": 62.50,
      "documented": true,
      "proof": "geo-fence-timestamps + BOL-scan"
    },
    {
      "type": "detention_delivery",
      "hours": 0.5,
      "rate": 50,
      "amount": 25.00,
      "documented": true,
      "proof": "geo-fence-timestamps"
    },
    {
      "type": "lumper",
      "amount": 75.00,
      "documented": true,
      "proof": "lumper-receipt-photo"
    }
  ],
  "total_accessorials": 162.50,
  "total_invoice": 862.50,
  "missing_documentation": []
}
```

---

## Accessorial Dispute Prevention

Best practices built into this skill:
1. **Pre-approve in writing** — all accessorials must be in RC before dispatch
2. **Notify broker in advance** — detention alerts give broker chance to respond
3. **Timestamp everything** — geo-fence is objective proof
4. **Get BOL documentation** — facility-stamped times are strongest evidence
5. **Save all communications** — broker emails/texts agreeing to accessorials

---

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Lumper receipt lost | Contact lumper company for copy; note in file |
| Broker denies detention was authorized | Provide RC + timestamps; escalate if refused |
| Driver didn't get BOL times stamped | Use geo-fence + text message proof as backup |
| RC has no accessorial clause | Attempt claim citing industry standard; note for future |
| Broker says accessorial not in budget | Accessorials in RC are contractual obligations — insist |


---


# DOMAIN 6 - ADVANCED OPERATIONS (Skills CC-JJ)

---
skill_id: "CC-emergency-rebrokering"

  - delivery_deadline: "when freight MUST arrive"
outputs:

  - replacement_carrier: "dict with carrier details"

# SKILL: Emergency Rebrokering
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: Carrier breakdown or any situation that threatens freight delivery.
**Phase**: 13
**Priority**: CRITICAL — hardest scenario in dispatching; every minute costs money

---

## Purpose

When a carrier breaks down mid-load, find a replacement truck and get the freight moving again within 2 hours. Simultaneously manage broker expectations and protect the relationship.

---

## Emergency Response Timeline

| Time | Action |
|------|--------|
| T+0 | Emergency detected → all actions start simultaneously |
| T+2 min | Broker notified with status and estimated resolution time |
| T+5 min | Emergency truck search launched on DAT + calls to carriers in area |
| T+30 min | If no replacement found, escalate search radius and rate |
| T+60 min | Human operator must take over if no replacement |
| T+120 min | Maximum autonomous resolution window |

---

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Immediate Broker Notification

```python
async def notify_broker_emergency(load: dict, emergency: dict):
    # Call broker immediately — this cannot wait
    await bland_ai.call(
        phone=load.broker_contact_phone,
        script=f"""
        This is [Dispatcher] calling about load {load.broker_ref}. 
        We have an emergency — our driver has {emergency['description']} at 
        {emergency['location']}. I am actively working on a replacement truck right now 
        and will update you every 30 minutes. The freight is secure. 
        Please advise if the delivery window has any flexibility.
        What is the latest the receiver can accept delivery?
        """
    )
    
    # Also send email immediately
    await send_email(
        to=load.broker_email,
        subject=f"EMERGENCY UPDATE — Load {load.broker_ref}",
        body=f"""
I want to give you immediate notification of an issue with load {load.broker_ref}.

Situation: {emergency['description']}
Location: {emergency['location']}  
Freight status: Secure/Safe
Time of incident: {emergency['timestamp']}

I am actively sourcing a replacement carrier in the area right now.
I will update you every 30 minutes until resolved.
Estimated resolution: within 2 hours.

If delivery window needs adjustment, please contact the receiver now.

{DISPATCHER_SIGNATURE}
        """
    )
```

### Step 2 — Emergency Truck Search

```python
async def find_replacement_truck(load: dict, emergency: dict) -> dict:
    current_location = emergency["current_location"]
    
    # Search expanding radii simultaneously
    search_tasks = await asyncio.gather(
        search_dat_emergency(current_location, 50, load),    # 50 mile radius
        search_truckstop_emergency(current_location, 50, load),
        search_internal_carriers(current_location, 100, load),  # Our own carrier base
    )
    
    # Flatten and rank by proximity + equipment match
    candidates = []
    for results in search_tasks:
        candidates.extend(results)
    
    # Sort by: (1) distance to current location, (2) equipment match, (3) rate
    candidates.sort(key=lambda c: c["distance_miles"])
    
    return candidates[:10]  # Top 10 candidates

async def search_internal_carriers(location: dict, radius_miles: int, load: dict) -> list:
    """Check our own carrier base first — faster relationship + known quality"""
    carriers = await db.get_available_carriers(
        equipment=load.equipment_type,
        available_now=True,
        near_location=location,
        radius_miles=radius_miles,
    )
    
    return [
        {
            "type": "internal_carrier",
            "carrier_id": c.id,
            "name": c.company_name,
            "phone": c.driver_phone,
            "distance_miles": c.distance_to_location,
            "equipment": c.equipment_type,
            "known_quality": True,
        }
        for c in carriers
    ]
```

### Step 3 — Emergency Rate Authorization

```python
EMERGENCY_RATE_PREMIUMS = {
    "perishable_cargo": 1.50,     # 50% premium — cargo will be lost
    "high_value_cargo": 1.40,     # 40% premium
    "standard_cargo": 1.25,       # 25% premium — still urgent
    "appointment_critical": 1.35, # 35% premium — buyer will refuse late delivery
}

async def calculate_emergency_rate(load: dict) -> dict:
    base_rate = load.market_rate_per_mile
    
    if load.freight_perishable:
        premium = EMERGENCY_RATE_PREMIUMS["perishable_cargo"]
    elif abs((datetime.fromisoformat(load.delivery_appointment) - datetime.utcnow()).hours) < 4:
        premium = EMERGENCY_RATE_PREMIUMS["appointment_critical"]
    else:
        premium = EMERGENCY_RATE_PREMIUMS["standard_cargo"]
    
    emergency_rate = base_rate * premium
    
    # Cost impact to our business (we absorb or bill broker)
    original_rate = load.agreed_rate_per_mile
    additional_cost = (emergency_rate - original_rate) * load.remaining_miles
    
    return {
        "emergency_rate": emergency_rate,
        "original_rate": original_rate,
        "additional_cost": additional_cost,
        "recoverable_from_broker": load.rc_force_majeure_clause,
    }
```

### Step 4 — Rapid Replacement Booking

```python
async def book_replacement_carrier(candidate: dict, load: dict, emergency_rate: dict):
    # Call replacement carrier immediately
    call_result = await bland_ai.call(
        phone=candidate["phone"],
        script=f"""
        Hi, this is [Dispatcher] — I have an emergency load situation. 
        I have a {load.equipment_type} load in {emergency['location']}, 
        {load.remaining_miles} miles remaining to {load.destination}.
        The freight is ready right now — our carrier broke down. 
        I can offer ${emergency_rate['emergency_rate']:.2f}/mile.
        Can you cover this today? I need a yes or no right now.
        """,
        max_duration_seconds=120,  # 2-minute call max
    )
    
    if call_result["outcome"] == "BOOKED":
        # Fast-track the paperwork — abbreviated packet process
        await fast_track_dispatch(candidate, load)
        return {"success": True, "carrier": candidate}
    
    return {"success": False}

async def fast_track_dispatch(carrier: dict, load: dict):
    """Emergency dispatch — skip normal packet cycle, verify MC only"""
    
    # Quick MC verification (3-minute check)
    fmcsa = await fmcsa_api.quick_lookup(carrier["mc_number"])
    if fmcsa["status"] != "ACTIVE":
        raise Exception("Replacement carrier not ACTIVE on FMCSA")
    
    # Email simplified dispatch sheet immediately
    await send_dispatch_sheet(carrier, load, emergency=True)
    
    # Notify broker of replacement carrier
    await notify_broker_replacement(load, carrier)
    
    # Log emergency rebook
    await db.log_emergency_rebroker(load.id, carrier, "BREAKDOWN")
```

---

## Cargo Transfer (If Truck Can't Continue)

If breakdown requires transferring freight to a new truck:

```python
async def coordinate_cargo_transfer(load: dict, breakdown_location: dict):
    # Find nearest truck stop with space
    transfer_location = await google_maps.find_nearest(
        location=breakdown_location,
        type="truck_stop",
        requires_parking=True,
    )
    
    # Guide breakdown driver to safe location
    await send_whatsapp(
        load.driver_phone,
        f"Navigate to: {transfer_location['name']}, {transfer_location['address']}. "
        f"Replacement truck will meet you there. Secure freight. Don't leave the vehicle."
    )
    
    # Update replacement carrier with transfer location
    # ...
```

---

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| No replacement found in 60 min | Human operator takes over immediately |
| Perishable cargo at risk >4 hours | Contact shipper for guidance; consider storage options |
| Broker won't accept late delivery | Escalate; document force majeure |
| Driver abandons truck | Contact law enforcement; Z-cargo-theft-response |

skill_id: "DD-reefer-temp-monitoring"

  - claim_protection_status: "bool — continuous record maintained"

# SKILL: Reefer Temperature Monitoring
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: Any reefer load dispatched.
**Phase**: 13
**Priority**: HIGH

---

## Purpose

Continuously log reefer temperature and alert instantly when it goes out of range. Protect carrier from cargo claims by proving continuous compliance. Protect commodity integrity.

---

## Temperature Requirements by Commodity

| Commodity | Min °F | Max °F | Tolerance | Alert Level |
|-----------|--------|--------|-----------|-------------|
| Fresh produce | 34 | 40 | ±2°F | WARNING at ±1°F |
| Frozen foods | -10 | 0 | ±3°F | CRITICAL at ±2°F |
| Dairy | 34 | 38 | ±2°F | WARNING at ±1°F |
| Pharmaceuticals | 36 | 46 | ±2°F | CRITICAL at ±1°F |
| Ice cream | -20 | -5 | ±5°F | CRITICAL at ±3°F |
| Meat (fresh) | 28 | 34 | ±2°F | CRITICAL at ±1°F |
| Flowers | 33 | 38 | ±2°F | WARNING at ±1°F |

---

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Pre-Trip Temperature Verification

```python
async def verify_reefer_precool(load_id: str, required_temp: dict) -> bool:
    """Confirm trailer is at correct temp BEFORE loading"""
    current_temp = await get_reefer_temp(load_id)
    
    if current_temp > required_temp["max"] + 2:
        # Not yet precooled — alert driver
        await send_whatsapp(
            load.driver_phone,
            f"🌡️ PRECOOL CHECK: Trailer is at {current_temp}°F. "
            f"Required: {required_temp['min']}–{required_temp['max']}°F. "
            f"DO NOT load until temperature reaches {required_temp['min']}°F. "
            f"Estimated time to target temp: {estimate_cooldown_time(current_temp, required_temp['min'])} min."
        )
        return False
    
    return True
```

### Step 2 — Continuous Monitoring Loop

```python
async def monitor_reefer_temp(load_id: str):
    """Runs every 15 minutes while load is in transit"""
    
    load = await db.get_load(load_id)
    required = load.temp_requirements
    
    while load.status not in ["DELIVERED", "CANCELLED"]:
        # Pull current temperature from reefer unit
        temp_reading = await reefer_api.get_current_temp(load.reefer_unit_id)
        
        # Log reading
        await db.insert("reefer_temp_log", {
            "load_id": load_id,
            "timestamp": datetime.utcnow().isoformat(),
            "temperature": temp_reading["current_temp"],
            "setpoint": temp_reading["setpoint"],
            "reefer_status": temp_reading["unit_status"],  # RUNNING | DEFROST | OFF
            "fuel_level": temp_reading.get("fuel_level"),
        })
        
        # Check for violations
        current_temp = temp_reading["current_temp"]
        
        if current_temp < required["min"] - required["alert_threshold"]:
            await handle_temp_alert(load_id, current_temp, required, "TOO_COLD")
        elif current_temp > required["max"] + required["alert_threshold"]:
            await handle_temp_alert(load_id, current_temp, required, "TOO_WARM")
        
        # Check reefer unit status
        if temp_reading["unit_status"] == "OFF":
            await send_whatsapp(
                load.driver_phone,
                f"🚨 REEFER UNIT IS OFF! Turn on immediately. "
                f"Required temp: {required['min']}–{required['max']}°F. "
                f"Current: {current_temp}°F."
            )
        
        await asyncio.sleep(900)  # 15-minute intervals
```

### Step 3 — Alert Protocols

```python
async def handle_temp_alert(load_id: str, current_temp: float, required: dict, alert_type: str):
    load = await db.get_load(load_id)
    
    severity = "WARNING" if abs(current_temp - required["target"]) < 3 else "CRITICAL"
    
    # Alert driver
    await send_whatsapp(
        load.driver_phone,
        f"{'⚠️' if severity == 'WARNING' else '🚨'} TEMP ALERT: "
        f"Reefer showing {current_temp}°F. "
        f"Required range: {required['min']}–{required['max']}°F. "
        f"Check reefer unit setting and fuel level immediately. "
        f"Reply with status update."
    )
    
    if severity == "CRITICAL":
        # Alert broker
        await send_email(
            to=load.broker_email,
            subject=f"Temperature Alert — Load {load.broker_ref}",
            body=f"Proactive notice: temperature reading of {current_temp}°F was detected. "
                 f"Driver has been alerted and is checking unit. Monitoring continuously.",
        )
        
        # Escalate to human
        await human_escalation.create(
            reason="REEFER_TEMP_CRITICAL",
            context={"load_id": load_id, "current_temp": current_temp, "required": required},
            urgency="P1",
        )
```

### Step 4 — Generate Temperature Report at Delivery

```python
async def generate_temp_report(load_id: str) -> bytes:
    """PDF with full temperature log — protects against cargo claims"""
    
    temp_log = await db.get_temp_log(load_id)
    
    report_data = {
        "load_id": load_id,
        "total_readings": len(temp_log),
        "min_temp_recorded": min(r["temperature"] for r in temp_log),
        "max_temp_recorded": max(r["temperature"] for r in temp_log),
        "avg_temp": statistics.mean(r["temperature"] for r in temp_log),
        "out_of_range_events": [r for r in temp_log if r.get("alert")],
        "continuous_monitoring": True,
        "monitoring_interval_minutes": 15,
        "full_log": temp_log,
    }
    
    pdf = generate_temp_report_pdf(report_data)
    
    # Attach to load record for dispute protection
    s3_path = f"loads/{load_id}/temperature-report.pdf"
    await s3.upload(s3_path, pdf)
    
    return pdf
```

outputs:

  - overweight_warnings: "states where load may exceed limits"
  - bypass_instructions: "driver instructions for each weigh station"
  - permit_requirements: "if overweight permits needed"

  - PrePass API

  - TMS
  - WhatsApp (driver notifications)

# SKILL: Scale & PrePass Management
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: Every load dispatch.
**Phase**: 12 (concurrent with dispatch)
**Priority**: HIGH

---

## Purpose

Maximize weigh station bypass opportunities to save driver time and reduce compliance risk. Alert drivers to potential overweight situations before they reach a scale.

---

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Route Weigh Station Mapping

```python
async def map_route_weigh_stations(route: dict, load: dict) -> list:
    # Get all weigh stations along route via HERE Maps truck data
    stations = await here_maps.get_weigh_stations(
        route=route["waypoints"],
        vehicle_type="truck",
    )
    
    # Get PrePass/Drivewyze eligibility for carrier
    carrier_bypass_status = await prepass_api.get_carrier_status(
        load.carrier.prepass_account_id
    )
    
    station_plan = []
    for station in stations:
        # Check if carrier is eligible for bypass
        bypass_eligible = carrier_bypass_status.get("eligible_states", [])
        can_bypass = station["state"] in bypass_eligible
        
        # Check weight against station threshold
        estimated_gvw = load.weight_lbs + load.carrier.truck_weight + load.carrier.trailer_weight
        station_limit = station.get("weight_limit", 80000)
        
        overweight_risk = estimated_gvw > station_limit * 0.95  # Alert at 95% of limit
        
        station_plan.append({
            "station_name": station["name"],
            "location": station["location"],
            "state": station["state"],
            "can_bypass": can_bypass and not overweight_risk,
            "overweight_risk": overweight_risk,
            "estimated_gvw": estimated_gvw,
            "station_limit": station_limit,
            "driver_instruction": generate_station_instruction(can_bypass, overweight_risk),
        })
    
    return station_plan

def generate_station_instruction(can_bypass: bool, overweight_risk: bool) -> str:
    if overweight_risk:
        return "⚠️ ENTER SCALE — Weight may exceed limit. Be prepared to pull in."
    elif can_bypass:
        return "✅ GREEN LIGHT LIKELY — PrePass should bypass. Watch for green transponder light."
    else:
        return "🔵 PULL IN — Enter scale normally."
```

### Step 2 — Real-Time Bypass Monitoring

```python
async def monitor_prepass_bypass(load_id: str):
    """Drivewyze webhook notifies us of actual bypass decisions"""
    
    # Register for bypass notifications
    await drivewyze_api.register_load(
        load_id=load_id,
        vehicle_id=load.carrier.vehicle_id,
        route=load.route,
    )

async def handle_bypass_notification(webhook: dict):
    """Called when driver approaches a scale"""
    
    decision = webhook["bypass_decision"]  # BYPASS | PULL_IN
    station = webhook["station_name"]
    
    if decision == "PULL_IN":
        # Alert driver immediately
        await send_whatsapp(
            load.driver_phone,
            f"⚖️ SCALE ALERT: Pull in at {station}. "
            f"Wait for officer inspection if required. "
            f"Keep all documents ready: registration, insurance, IFTA."
        )
        
        # Log in TMS
        await db.log_event(load_id, "WEIGH_STATION_PULL_IN", {"station": station})
```

### Step 3 — Overweight Alert

```python
async def check_overweight_risk(load: dict) -> dict:
    gvw = load.weight_lbs + load.carrier.tare_weight
    
    # Federal limit
    federal_limit = 80000  # lbs
    
    overweight_states = []
    
    # Check state-specific limits for route
    route_states = await get_states_on_route(load.route)
    
    for state in route_states:
        state_limit = STATE_WEIGHT_LIMITS.get(state, federal_limit)
        
        if gvw > state_limit:
            overweight_states.append({
                "state": state,
                "load_weight": gvw,
                "state_limit": state_limit,
                "overage": gvw - state_limit,
                "permit_required": True,
            })
    
    if overweight_states:
        # Trigger permit management skill
        await permit_management.request_permits(load.id, overweight_states)
        
        # Alert driver
        await send_whatsapp(
            load.driver_phone,
            f"⚠️ WEIGHT ALERT: Estimated GVW {gvw:,} lbs may exceed limits in: "
            f"{', '.join(s['state'] for s in overweight_states)}. "
            f"Permits being arranged. Do not proceed without permit confirmation."
        )
    
    return {"overweight_states": overweight_states}
```

skill_id: "FF-permit-management"
name: "Permit Management"

phase: 5
priority: medium
trigger: "Overweight or oversize load identified. Also triggered when load dimensions exceed standard limits."
inputs:

  - overweight_states: "list of states requiring permits"
  - load_dimensions: "width, height, length, weight"
  - route: "planned route"
  - move_date: "pickup/delivery dates"
outputs:
  - permits_obtained: "list of permits by state with permit numbers"
  - routing_requirements: "any mandatory routes, escort requirements"
  - cost: "total permit fees"
  - estimated_processing_time: "hours until permits ready"
integrations:
  - State DOT permit portals (automated where available)
  - TMS
  - Email (permit delivery)
depends_on: ["05-load-board-search", "EE-scale-prepass-management"]
triggers_next: ["13-driver-dispatch"]
tags: [permits, oversize, overweight, superload, state-permit, routing, compliance]
---

# SKILL: Permit Management
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: Non-standard load dimensions or weight.
**Phase**: 5 (pre-dispatch)
**Priority**: MEDIUM

---

## Purpose

Automatically apply for oversize/overweight permits so drivers never get caught at a scale without proper paperwork.

---

## Standard Permit Thresholds

| Dimension | Standard | Permit Required |
|-----------|---------|----------------|
| Width | 8.5 ft | >8.5 ft requires permit |
| Height | 13.5–14 ft (varies by state) | >14 ft most states |
| Length (truck+trailer) | 65 ft most states | >65 ft varies |
| Weight (GVW) | 80,000 lbs federal | >80,000 lbs per axle |

---

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Determine Permit Requirements

```python
async def assess_permit_needs(load: dict) -> list:
    required_permits = []
    
    dimensions = {
        "width": load.cargo_width_ft,
        "height": load.cargo_height_ft,
        "length": load.cargo_length_ft,
        "gvw": load.gross_vehicle_weight,
    }
    
    route_states = await get_states_on_route(load.route)
    
    for state in route_states:
        state_limits = STATE_PERMIT_THRESHOLDS[state]
        
        for dim, value in dimensions.items():
            limit = state_limits.get(dim, DEFAULT_LIMITS[dim])
            if value > limit:
                required_permits.append({
                    "state": state,
                    "dimension": dim,
                    "value": value,
                    "limit": limit,
                    "overage": value - limit,
                })
    
    return required_permits
```

### Step 2 — Automated Permit Filing

```python
AUTOMATED_STATE_PORTALS = {
    "TX": "https://apps.txdot.gov/apps/OverweightOversize/",
    "FL": "https://www.fdot.gov/maintenance/permits",
    "OH": "https://www.ops.ohio.gov",
    "IN": "https://www.in.gov/permits",
    # ... 20+ states with web portal automation
}

async def file_permit_automated(state: str, load: dict, requirements: dict) -> dict:
    portal = AUTOMATED_STATE_PORTALS.get(state)
    
    if portal:
        # Use Selenium/Playwright to fill portal forms
        permit_result = await portal_automation.file_permit({
            "state": state,
            "portal_url": portal,
            "carrier_mc": load.carrier.mc_number,
            "cargo_dimensions": requirements,
            "route": load.route,
            "move_date": load.pickup_date,
        })
        
        return permit_result
    else:
        # Email application for states without portals
        return await file_permit_by_email(state, load, requirements)
```

---
---
skill_id: "GG-multi-carrier-load-matching"
name: "Multi-Carrier Load Matching Optimizer"

phase: 4
priority: high
trigger: "Multiple carriers available simultaneously with multiple loads to cover. Runs when 2+ carriers are searching."
inputs:

  - available_loads: "array of eligible loads from load boards"
  - optimization_objective: "MAXIMIZE_FLEET_REVENUE | MINIMIZE_DEADHEAD | MAXIMIZE_BOOKINGS"

  - optimal_assignments: "carrier-to-load pairings that maximize objective"
  - total_fleet_revenue: "projected weekly gross"
  - deadhead_minimized: "total empty miles saved"
  - unmatched_carriers: "carriers with no good loads available"
  - unmatched_loads: "loads with no available carriers"
integrations:
  - TMS
  - DAT Rate Analytics API
  - Google Maps API (distance calculations)
  - Python scipy (optimization algorithm)

# SKILL: Multi-Carrier Load Matching Optimizer
## Cortex Bot — Truck Dispatch Automation

**Trigger**: 2+ carriers available simultaneously.
**Phase**: 4
**Priority**: HIGH

---

## Purpose

When managing 50 carriers simultaneously, naive "first come first served" load assignment leaves significant money on the table. This optimizer assigns loads to carriers to maximize total fleet revenue, not just individual load revenue.

---

## Optimization Problem Formulation

```python
"""
Given:
  - Set of available carriers C = {c1, c2, ..., cn}
  - Set of available loads L = {l1, l2, ..., lm}
  - Revenue matrix R[i][j] = expected revenue if carrier ci covers load lj
  - Feasibility matrix F[i][j] = 1 if carrier ci can physically cover load lj

Find:
  - Assignment A where A[i][j] = 1 if ci is assigned to lj
  - Maximize: SUM(R[i][j] * A[i][j]) for all i,j
  - Constraint: Each carrier assigned to at most 1 load
  - Constraint: Each load covered by at most 1 carrier
  - Constraint: A[i][j] = 0 where F[i][j] = 0

This is the classic Assignment Problem — solved optimally in O(n³) via
the Hungarian Algorithm (scipy.optimize.linear_sum_assignment)
"""

from scipy.optimize import linear_sum_assignment
import numpy as np

async def optimize_fleet_assignments(carriers: list, loads: list) -> list:
    n_carriers = len(carriers)
    n_loads = len(loads)
    
    # Build revenue matrix
    revenue_matrix = np.zeros((n_carriers, n_loads))
    
    for i, carrier in enumerate(carriers):
        for j, load in enumerate(loads):
            # Check feasibility first
            if not is_feasible(carrier, load):
                revenue_matrix[i][j] = -999999  # Infeasible
                continue
            
            # Calculate expected revenue for this pairing
            revenue = await calculate_expected_revenue(carrier, load)
            revenue_matrix[i][j] = revenue
    
    # Solve assignment problem
    # linear_sum_assignment minimizes, so negate for maximization
    row_ind, col_ind = linear_sum_assignment(-revenue_matrix)
    
    # Build assignment results
    assignments = []
    for carrier_idx, load_idx in zip(row_ind, col_ind):
        if revenue_matrix[carrier_idx][load_idx] > 0:  # Only include valid assignments
            assignments.append({
                "carrier": carriers[carrier_idx],
                "load": loads[load_idx],
                "expected_revenue": revenue_matrix[carrier_idx][load_idx],
            })
    
    return assignments

async def calculate_expected_revenue(carrier: dict, load: dict) -> float:
    # Deadhead cost
    deadhead_miles = await google_maps.distance(carrier["current_location"], load["pickup"])
    deadhead_cost = deadhead_miles * 0.35
    
    # Market rate estimate
    market_rate = await dat_api.get_rate(load["origin"], load["destination"], load["equipment"])
    
    # Carrier rate floor check
    if market_rate < carrier["rate_floor"]:
        return 0  # Below floor — don't assign
    
    # Expected gross revenue
    gross = market_rate * load["loaded_miles"]
    
    # Reload market quality bonus (positioning value)
    reload_score = await dat_api.get_load_to_truck_ratio(load["destination"])
    position_bonus = reload_score * 10  # $10 per point
    
    # Net expected value
    net = gross - deadhead_cost + position_bonus
    
    return net

def is_feasible(carrier: dict, load: dict) -> bool:
    """Quick feasibility check"""
    return (
        carrier["equipment_type"] == load["equipment_type"]
        and carrier["max_weight"] >= load["weight"]
        and carrier["available_at"] <= load["pickup_datetime"]
        and carrier.get("no_hazmat") is False or load.get("hazmat") is False
    )
```


# SKILL HH — Dedicated Lane Management
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "HH-dedicated-lane-management"
name: "Dedicated Lane Management"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 2
priority: medium
trigger: "Carrier signs dedicated lane agreement OR weekly review of all active dedicated relationships"
inputs:
  - carrier_id: "string"
  - shipper_id: "string"
  - lane_contract: "origin, destination, guaranteed volume, rate, duration"
outputs:
  - lane_performance_report: "weekly KPIs for dedicated relationship"
  - capacity_alerts: "when carrier cannot fulfill guaranteed volume"
  - renewal_recommendation: "should contract be extended, renegotiated, or ended"
integrations:
  - TMS
  - Email (shipper relationship)
  - Calendar (contract renewal alerts)
depends_on: ["04-carrier-profile-management", "MM-shipper-direct-outreach"]
triggers_next: ["25-carrier-performance-scoring"]
tags: [dedicated, contract, shipper, guaranteed-volume, lane-management]
---

## Purpose

Manage carriers who have dedicated shipper relationships with guaranteed weekly volume. These carriers operate differently from spot market carriers — they have contracted rates, guaranteed loads, and require relationship management with the shipper, not just load board searching.

## What Is a Dedicated Lane?

A dedicated lane is a contract between a carrier and a shipper (or broker acting on shipper's behalf) for:
- **Fixed origin → destination** (e.g., Nashville TN → Atlanta GA every Monday/Wednesday/Friday)
- **Guaranteed volume** (e.g., 3 loads/week guaranteed)
- **Contracted rate** (e.g., $2.65/mile, locked for 6 months)
- **Mutual commitment** — carrier commits capacity, shipper commits volume

## Dedicated vs Spot Market Comparison

| Attribute | Dedicated Lane | Spot Market |
|-----------|---------------|-------------|
| Rate stability | Fixed | Volatile |
| Load certainty | Guaranteed | Must search daily |
| Dispatcher effort | Low (no search) | High (daily search) |
| Rate vs market | Usually 5–10% below peak | At market |
| Carrier planning | Easy (predictable) | Hard (daily changes) |
| Best for | Consistent earners | High-rate hunters |

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Dedicated Lane Onboarding

When carrier enters dedicated relationship:

```json
{
  "dedicated_lane_id": "DED-2026-001",
  "carrier_id": "CARR-032026-001",
  "shipper_id": "SHIP-ECHO-001",
  "origin": "Nashville, TN",
  "destination": "Atlanta, GA",
  "equipment": "53_dry_van",
  "rate_per_mile": 2.65,
  "guaranteed_loads_per_week": 3,
  "load_days": ["Monday", "Wednesday", "Friday"],
  "pickup_window": "07:00-10:00",
  "contract_start": "2026-04-01",
  "contract_end": "2026-09-30",
  "rate_escalator": "5% on Oct 1 renewal",
  "shipper_contact": "logistics@shipper.com",
  "notice_period_days": 30
}
```

### Step 2 — Weekly Load Execution (Automated)

On each contracted load day:
1. Auto-generate load record from dedicated lane template (no search needed)
2. Send pre-formatted dispatch sheet to driver (same template each week)
3. Skip broker negotiation — rate is pre-contracted
4. Skip FMCSA/credit checks — relationship is already verified
5. Execute normally from Phase 12 (dispatch) onward

```python
async def execute_dedicated_load(lane_id: str, pickup_date: date):
    lane = await get_dedicated_lane(lane_id)
    
    # Auto-create load record from template
    load = await create_load_from_template(
        template=lane,
        pickup_date=pickup_date,
        load_id=f"DED-{lane_id}-{pickup_date.isoformat()}"
    )
    
    # Skip straight to dispatch (no search/negotiate needed)
    await driver_dispatch_skill(load)
    logger.info(f"Dedicated load {load.load_id} auto-dispatched for {pickup_date}")
```

### Step 3 — Volume Compliance Tracking

Monitor whether shipper is delivering guaranteed volume:

```python
def check_volume_compliance(lane_id: str, week_of: date):
    committed = lane.guaranteed_loads_per_week
    actual = count_loads_tendered(lane_id, week_of)
    
    shortfall = committed - actual
    
    if shortfall > 0:
        # Shipper failed to tender guaranteed volume
        notify_shipper(
            f"We had {committed - actual} truck(s) available this week per our agreement "
            f"but did not receive tender. Per the contract, a TONU of $150 applies to each missed load."
        )
        generate_tonu_invoice(lane_id, shortfall, week_of)
```

### Step 4 — Carrier Capacity Availability Check

If carrier cannot run a committed load day:
1. Alert 48 hours in advance (driver personal day, equipment issue)
2. Attempt to find backup carrier for same lane
3. Notify shipper as early as possible
4. Log capacity miss — 3 misses in 90 days triggers contract review

### Step 5 — Contract Renewal Analysis (60 Days Before Expiry)

```python
def generate_renewal_recommendation(lane_id: str):
    lane = get_dedicated_lane(lane_id)
    performance = get_lane_performance(lane_id, last_6_months=True)
    market = get_dat_market_rate(lane.origin, lane.destination)
    
    contracted_rate = lane.rate_per_mile
    market_rate = market.avg_7day
    
    recommendation = {}
    
    if performance.on_time_delivery_pct >= 97 and performance.volume_compliance >= 95:
        if contracted_rate < market_rate * 0.95:
            recommendation = {
                "action": "RENEGOTIATE",
                "reason": "Excellent performance but rate is 5%+ below market",
                "suggested_rate": market_rate * 0.97
            }
        else:
            recommendation = {"action": "RENEW", "reason": "Strong performance, rate at market"}
    elif performance.volume_compliance < 85:
        recommendation = {
            "action": "TERMINATE",
            "reason": "Shipper delivered <85% of committed volume",
            "give_notice_date": date.today()
        }
    
    return recommendation
```

### Step 6 — Weekly Lane Performance Report

Send to shipper every Monday:
```
DEDICATED LANE WEEKLY REPORT
Lane: Nashville TN → Atlanta GA | Week: Mar 16–22, 2026

Loads Committed: 3 | Loads Tendered: 3 | Loads Delivered: 3
On-Time Pickup: 100% | On-Time Delivery: 100%
Detention Events: 0
Carrier: ABC Trucking | MC#: XXXXXX

Notes: No issues this week. Excellent performance.
```

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Shipper tenders more than contracted volume | Evaluate as spot load; book at market rate |
| Carrier requests rate increase mid-contract | Log request; negotiate at next renewal |
| Shipper cancels contract early | Invoke termination clause; calculate TONU for notice period |
| Dedicated carrier breaks down | Emergency rebrokering (Skill CC) with shipper notification |

# SKILL II — Multi-Stop Route Optimization
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "II-multi-stop-optimization"
name: "Multi-Stop Route Optimization"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 4
priority: medium
trigger: "Load has 2+ pickup or delivery stops. Triggered during load triage before broker call."
inputs:
  - stops: "array of pickup/delivery addresses with appointment windows"
  - truck_location: "current carrier GPS position"
  - hos_remaining: "driver hours of service available"
outputs:
  - optimized_sequence: "stops in best order with ETAs"
  - total_route_miles: "float"
  - appointment_feasibility: "boolean — can all appointments be met?"
  - appointment_risk_flags: "any stops where timing is tight"
integrations:
  - Google Maps Platform (Distance Matrix API)
  - HERE Maps (truck-specific routing)
  - TMS
depends_on: ["06-load-triage-eligibility"]
triggers_next: ["08-broker-negotiation", "13-driver-dispatch"]
tags: [multi-stop, route-optimization, appointments, sequencing]
---

## Purpose

When a load has multiple pickup or delivery stops, find the optimal sequence to minimize total drive time, meet all appointment windows, and stay within HOS limits. A poor sequence can add 50–150 miles and cause appointment misses.

## Stop Types

| Type | Description | Sequencing Rule |
|------|-------------|-----------------|
| Pickup → Delivery | Standard: pick up at A, deliver to B | Sequential only |
| Multi-Pickup | Pick up at A and B, deliver to C | Optimize A↔B order |
| Multi-Delivery | Pick up at A, deliver to B and C | Optimize B↔C order |
| Full Multi-Stop | Pick up at A and B, deliver to C and D | Full TSP solve |

## Algorithm

### Step 1 — Parse Appointment Constraints

```python
@dataclass
class Stop:
    stop_id: str
    type: str  # "pickup" | "delivery"
    address: str
    latitude: float
    longitude: float
    earliest_arrival: datetime
    latest_arrival: datetime
    dwell_estimate_hours: float  # 1.5hr pickup, 2hr delivery avg

def parse_stops(broker_load_details: dict) -> List[Stop]:
    stops = []
    for s in broker_load_details['stops']:
        stops.append(Stop(
            stop_id=s['ref'],
            type=s['type'],
            address=s['address'],
            latitude=s['lat'],
            longitude=s['lng'],
            earliest_arrival=parse_datetime(s['appointment_open']),
            latest_arrival=parse_datetime(s['appointment_close']),
            dwell_estimate_hours=1.5 if s['type'] == 'pickup' else 2.0
        ))
    return stops
```

### Step 2 — Build Distance Matrix

```python
async def build_distance_matrix(stops: List[Stop], origin: tuple) -> np.ndarray:
    """Get drive times between all stop pairs via Google Maps Distance Matrix."""
    
    all_points = [origin] + [(s.latitude, s.longitude) for s in stops]
    n = len(all_points)
    matrix = np.zeros((n, n))
    
    # Google Maps Distance Matrix API (batch request)
    result = await maps_client.distance_matrix(
        origins=all_points,
        destinations=all_points,
        mode="driving",
        departure_time=datetime.now(),
        traffic_model="best_guess"
    )
    
    for i, row in enumerate(result['rows']):
        for j, element in enumerate(row['elements']):
            matrix[i][j] = element['duration_in_traffic']['value'] / 3600  # hours
    
    return matrix
```

### Step 3 — Nearest Neighbor Heuristic (Fast, Good Enough for ≤8 Stops)

```python
def nearest_neighbor_tsp(distance_matrix: np.ndarray, stops: List[Stop]) -> List[int]:
    """
    Solve TSP with appointment window constraints using nearest neighbor heuristic.
    Respects pickup-before-delivery ordering constraints.
    """
    n = len(stops)
    unvisited = set(range(n))
    route = []
    current = 0  # Start from origin (index 0)
    current_time = datetime.now()
    
    while unvisited:
        best_next = None
        best_score = float('inf')
        
        for candidate in unvisited:
            # Check precedence: can't deliver before picking up same commodity
            if stops[candidate].type == 'delivery':
                paired_pickup_idx = find_paired_pickup(stops, candidate)
                if paired_pickup_idx in unvisited:
                    continue  # Can't deliver before picking up
            
            # Arrival time if we go here next
            travel_time = distance_matrix[current + 1][candidate + 1]
            arrival = current_time + timedelta(hours=travel_time)
            
            # Wait if early
            actual_arrival = max(arrival, stops[candidate].earliest_arrival)
            
            # Skip if we'd miss the latest appointment
            if actual_arrival > stops[candidate].latest_arrival:
                continue
            
            # Score = travel time + wait time
            wait_time = max(0, (stops[candidate].earliest_arrival - arrival).total_seconds() / 3600)
            score = travel_time + wait_time * 0.5  # Weight wait time less than drive time
            
            if score < best_score:
                best_score = score
                best_next = candidate
        
        if best_next is None:
            # No feasible next stop — appointment constraint violation
            return None  # Infeasible sequence
        
        route.append(best_next)
        current_time += timedelta(hours=distance_matrix[current + 1][best_next + 1])
        current_time = max(current_time, stops[best_next].earliest_arrival)
        current_time += timedelta(hours=stops[best_next].dwell_estimate_hours)
        current = best_next
        unvisited.remove(best_next)
    
    return route
```

### Step 4 — Generate Optimized Route Output

```python
def generate_route_plan(stops: List[Stop], sequence: List[int], distance_matrix: np.ndarray):
    plan = []
    current_time = datetime.now()
    total_miles = 0
    
    for i, stop_idx in enumerate(sequence):
        stop = stops[stop_idx]
        
        if i == 0:
            travel_hrs = distance_matrix[0][stop_idx + 1]
        else:
            prev_idx = sequence[i-1]
            travel_hrs = distance_matrix[prev_idx + 1][stop_idx + 1]
        
        arrival = current_time + timedelta(hours=travel_hrs)
        actual_arrival = max(arrival, stop.earliest_arrival)
        departure = actual_arrival + timedelta(hours=stop.dwell_estimate_hours)
        
        on_time = actual_arrival <= stop.latest_arrival
        tight = (stop.latest_arrival - actual_arrival).total_seconds() < 1800  # <30 min buffer
        
        plan.append({
            "sequence": i + 1,
            "stop_id": stop.stop_id,
            "type": stop.type,
            "address": stop.address,
            "drive_time_hours": round(travel_hrs, 2),
            "estimated_arrival": actual_arrival.isoformat(),
            "appointment_window": f"{stop.earliest_arrival.strftime('%H:%M')} – {stop.latest_arrival.strftime('%H:%M')}",
            "status": "ON_TIME" if on_time and not tight else "TIGHT" if on_time and tight else "LATE",
            "wait_time_minutes": max(0, (stop.earliest_arrival - arrival).total_seconds() / 60)
        })
        
        current_time = departure
        total_miles += travel_hrs * 55  # Estimate 55 mph avg
    
    return {
        "sequence": plan,
        "total_estimated_miles": int(total_miles),
        "total_drive_hours": sum(s["drive_time_hours"] for s in plan),
        "feasible": all(s["status"] != "LATE" for s in plan),
        "risk_flags": [s for s in plan if s["status"] == "TIGHT"]
    }
```

### Step 5 — HOS Feasibility Check

```python
def check_hos_feasibility(route_plan: dict, hos_remaining: float) -> bool:
    total_drive_hours = route_plan["total_drive_hours"]
    total_dwell_hours = sum(s.dwell_estimate_hours for s in stops)
    total_on_duty = total_drive_hours + total_dwell_hours
    
    # Check 11-hour drive limit
    if total_drive_hours > hos_remaining:
        return False, f"Requires {total_drive_hours:.1f} drive hours, only {hos_remaining:.1f} available"
    
    # Check 14-hour window
    if total_on_duty > 14:
        return False, f"Total on-duty time {total_on_duty:.1f} hrs exceeds 14-hour window"
    
    return True, "HOS OK"
```

## Output Example

```json
{
  "load_id": "TMS-2026-0412",
  "stop_count": 3,
  "optimized_sequence": [
    {
      "sequence": 1, "type": "pickup", "address": "123 Shipper A, Memphis TN",
      "estimated_arrival": "2026-03-21T08:15:00", "appointment_window": "07:00–10:00",
      "status": "ON_TIME", "drive_time_hours": 0.25
    },
    {
      "sequence": 2, "type": "pickup", "address": "456 Shipper B, Jackson TN",
      "estimated_arrival": "2026-03-21T10:05:00", "appointment_window": "09:30–11:30",
      "status": "ON_TIME", "drive_time_hours": 1.3
    },
    {
      "sequence": 3, "type": "delivery", "address": "789 Receiver, Atlanta GA",
      "estimated_arrival": "2026-03-21T16:45:00", "appointment_window": "15:00–18:00",
      "status": "ON_TIME", "drive_time_hours": 5.1
    }
  ],
  "total_estimated_miles": 420,
  "total_drive_hours": 6.65,
  "feasible": true,
  "risk_flags": []
}
```

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| No feasible sequence (appointment conflicts) | Flag load: "INFEASIBLE — appointment windows incompatible" |
| Google Maps timeout | Fall back to straight-line distance estimation |
| >8 stops | Use 2-opt improvement on nearest neighbor solution |
| HOS insufficient for route | Identify split point for 10-hour reset |

# SKILL JJ — Drop Trailer Management
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "JJ-drop-trailer-management"
name: "Drop Trailer Management"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 12
priority: medium
trigger: "Load type is drop_and_hook OR carrier has a trailer left at a facility"
inputs:
  - load_id: "string"
  - trailer_id: "string"
  - facility_id: "string"
  - drop_timestamp: "ISO 8601"
  - carrier_id: "string"
outputs:
  - trailer_status: "enum: IN_TRANSIT | DROPPED | AVAILABLE | OVERDUE"
  - dwell_hours: "float — time trailer has been at facility"
  - rental_fees_accrued: "float — if trailer overdue"
  - pickup_alert: "when carrier should retrieve trailer"
integrations:
  - TMS
  - Telematics/GPS API (trailer tracking if equipped)
  - WhatsApp/SMS (driver alerts)
  - Email (broker rental fee claims)
depends_on: ["13-driver-dispatch"]
triggers_next: ["27-accessorials-tracking"]
tags: [drop-trailer, hook, dwell, rental, trailer-pool, drop-and-hook]
---

## Purpose

Track every trailer that is dropped at a facility. Prevent excessive dwell time that results in rental fees from shippers, trailers getting stuck at facilities, and carriers losing equipment. Ensure drop & hook execution is smooth.

## Trailer Events

```
LOADED (carrier has trailer) 
  → DROPPED (left at shipper for loading)
    → LOADED (carrier picks up pre-loaded trailer)
      → DROPPED (left at receiver for unloading)
        → AVAILABLE (trailer retrieved, free for next load)
```

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Drop Event Trigger

When driver confirms trailer drop:
1. Log: `TRAILER_DROPPED` with facility, timestamp, GPS coordinates
2. Confirm: did driver drop correct trailer at correct facility?
3. Note any pre-existing damage (driver photo at drop)
4. Set dwell timer based on facility's free dwell window

### Step 2 — Dwell Time Monitoring

```python
FACILITY_FREE_DWELL = {
    "shipper": 24,    # Most shippers: 24 free hours for loading
    "receiver": 24,   # Most receivers: 24 free hours for unloading
    "broker_yard": 48,  # Broker yards: 48 hours typically free
    "default": 24
}

async def monitor_trailer_dwell(trailer_id: str):
    trailer = await get_trailer(trailer_id)
    facility_type = await get_facility_type(trailer.current_facility_id)
    
    free_hours = FACILITY_FREE_DWELL.get(facility_type, 24)
    dwell_hours = (datetime.utcnow() - trailer.dropped_at).total_seconds() / 3600
    
    if dwell_hours >= free_hours * 0.75:
        # Alert at 75% of free window
        await alert_driver(
            trailer.carrier_id,
            f"Trailer {trailer_id} has been at {trailer.facility_name} for {dwell_hours:.1f} hours. "
            f"Free dwell ends in {free_hours - dwell_hours:.1f} hours. "
            f"Please coordinate pickup."
        )
    
    if dwell_hours >= free_hours:
        # Dwell exceeded — fees begin
        await start_rental_fee_clock(trailer_id, rate=RENTAL_RATES.get(facility_type, 25))
        await notify_broker_of_dwell(trailer_id, dwell_hours)
```

### Step 3 — Rental Fee Tracking

```python
RENTAL_RATES = {
    # Per-day rates when trailer exceeds free dwell
    "shipper": 50,     # $50/day after free period
    "receiver": 50,
    "broker_yard": 75,
    "intermodal_ramp": 100  # Higher fees at rail yards
}

async def calculate_rental_fees(trailer_id: str) -> dict:
    trailer = await get_trailer(trailer_id)
    free_hours = get_free_dwell(trailer.facility_type)
    
    total_dwell = (datetime.utcnow() - trailer.dropped_at).total_seconds() / 3600
    billable_days = max(0, (total_dwell - free_hours) / 24)
    
    daily_rate = RENTAL_RATES.get(trailer.facility_type, 50)
    total_rental_fee = round(billable_days * daily_rate, 2)
    
    return {
        "trailer_id": trailer_id,
        "facility": trailer.facility_name,
        "total_dwell_hours": round(total_dwell, 1),
        "free_dwell_hours": free_hours,
        "billable_days": round(billable_days, 2),
        "daily_rate": daily_rate,
        "total_rental_fee": total_rental_fee
    }
```

### Step 4 — Drop & Hook Dispatch Coordination

For drop & hook loads (carrier picks up a pre-loaded trailer):
1. Confirm trailer number with broker before dispatch
2. Verify trailer is actually at the facility (GPS ping or broker confirmation)
3. Confirm trailer seal number matches RC
4. Include in dispatch sheet:
   ```
   DROP & HOOK:
   Trailer #: [X] (pre-loaded, waiting at dock)
   Seal #: [X] (verify before departure)
   Instructions: No waiting — trailer is ready. Call broker if trailer not found.
   ```

### Step 5 — Trailer Pool Dashboard

Track all carrier trailers simultaneously:

```
TRAILER POOL STATUS — March 20, 2026

Trailer 1234: AT SHIPPER (Memphis TN) | Dwell: 8.5 hrs | Free until 09:00 tomorrow ✅
Trailer 5678: IN TRANSIT (driver rolling) | Load: TMS-2026-0392 ✅  
Trailer 9012: AT RECEIVER (Atlanta GA) | Dwell: 26.2 hrs | ⚠️ OVERDUE 2.2 hrs | Rental: $4.58
Trailer 3456: AVAILABLE (Nashville TN) | Last drop: 3/19 | Ready for assignment ✅
```

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Wrong trailer dropped at wrong facility | Immediate broker call; coordinate correction |
| Trailer missing from facility | Alert carrier; check GPS; contact facility management |
| Facility charges rental fee on invoice | Document drop timestamp + GPS; dispute if within free window |
| Driver can't find pre-loaded trailer | Call broker immediately; verify trailer number and location |

# DOMAIN 7 - BUSINESS & GROWTH (Skills KK-NN)

# SKILL KK — Dispatch Pricing Strategy
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "KK-dispatch-pricing-strategy"
name: "Dispatch Pricing Strategy"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 0
priority: high
trigger: "New carrier onboarding (pricing conversation). Monthly review of all carrier pricing. Market analysis quarterly."
inputs:
  - carrier_id: "string (for individual pricing)"
  - market_data: "competitor pricing, industry benchmarks"
  - carrier_volume: "loads/week, gross revenue generated"
outputs:
  - recommended_fee_structure: "model + rate for this carrier"
  - competitive_positioning: "how our pricing compares to alternatives"
  - revenue_projection: "monthly income at recommended pricing"
integrations:
  - TMS (carrier revenue data)
  - CRM (carrier profile)
depends_on: ["02-carrier-onboarding"]
triggers_next: ["AA-service-agreement-generator", "Q-dispatcher-fee-collection"]
tags: [pricing, fee-structure, competitive, onboarding, revenue]
---

## Purpose

Set the right dispatch fee for each carrier relationship — high enough to be profitable, low enough to win and retain carriers. Price too high and carriers leave; too low and the business doesn't scale. This skill provides data-driven pricing recommendations.

## Market Benchmark (2026)

Based on industry research across TruckSmarter, Haulr, and independent dispatchers:

| Fee Model | Rate Range | Market Share | Best For |
|-----------|-----------|-------------|----------|
| Percentage of gross | 5–8% | ~60% of market | Variable volume carriers |
| Flat weekly fee | $300–650/week | ~25% of market | High-volume, predictable carriers |
| Hybrid (base + %) | $150/wk + 3% | ~10% of market | Aligns incentives |
| Per-load flat | $50–150/load | ~5% of market | Low-volume or new carriers |

## Pricing Decision Algorithm

```python
def recommend_pricing(carrier_profile: CarrierProfile) -> PricingRecommendation:
    
    # Step 1: Estimate carrier's weekly gross revenue
    avg_cpm = carrier_profile.target_rate_floor
    weekly_miles = 2500  # Average owner-operator
    estimated_weekly_gross = avg_cpm * weekly_miles
    
    # Step 2: Calculate fee at different models
    pct_fee = estimated_weekly_gross * 0.06  # 6% standard
    flat_fee = 450  # Mid-market flat fee
    hybrid_fee = 150 + (estimated_weekly_gross * 0.03)
    
    # Step 3: Carrier volume tier
    if carrier_profile.loads_per_week_estimate >= 5:
        volume_tier = "HIGH"
    elif carrier_profile.loads_per_week_estimate >= 3:
        volume_tier = "MEDIUM"
    else:
        volume_tier = "LOW"
    
    # Step 4: Recommend based on volume tier and carrier type
    if volume_tier == "HIGH" and estimated_weekly_gross > 7000:
        # High-volume, high-earning carrier: flat fee is better value for them
        return PricingRecommendation(
            model="flat_weekly",
            rate=550,
            monthly_revenue=2200,
            rationale="High-volume carrier — flat fee gives them certainty and us predictability"
        )
    elif volume_tier == "LOW":
        # New or low-volume carrier: percentage reduces their risk
        return PricingRecommendation(
            model="percentage",
            rate=0.07,  # 7% — higher rate for lower volume
            monthly_revenue=pct_fee * 4.3,
            rationale="Low-volume carrier — percentage aligns risk, we only earn when they haul"
        )
    else:
        # Standard carrier: hybrid gives both parties alignment
        return PricingRecommendation(
            model="percentage",
            rate=0.06,
            monthly_revenue=pct_fee * 4.3,
            rationale="Standard carrier — 6% percentage model, industry standard"
        )
```

## Pricing Conversation Script (New Carrier Onboarding)

```
"Let me walk you through how our fee structure works.

We charge [X]% of your gross load revenue per load. So if you haul a $1,200 load, 
our fee is $72. You keep $1,128 plus any detention or accessorials we collect for you.

Here's what that gets you: we handle every broker call, all the paperwork, 
negotiating the best rate, invoicing, and following up on payments. 
You just drive.

Most of our carriers earn $0.20–0.40/mile MORE per load than they were finding 
on their own, because we negotiate aggressively. On a 2,500-mile week, that's 
$500–1,000 more in your pocket even after our fee.

Any questions about how the fee works?"
```

## Volume Discounts

Reward high-performing, high-volume carriers to lock in retention:

| Weekly Loads | Standard Rate | Loyalty Discount |
|-------------|--------------|-----------------|
| 1–3 loads | 7% | — |
| 4–6 loads | 6% | 1% volume discount |
| 7+ loads | 5.5% | 1.5% volume discount |
| Dedicated + 10+ loads | 5% | Special rate for committed volume |

## Competitive Objection Handling

**"Another dispatcher charges only 5%"**
> "There are dispatchers who charge 5% and get you $2.10/mile. We charge 6% and get you $2.50/mile. On a 2,500-mile week, that's $1,000 more in your pocket versus $50 in fees. The question isn't the percentage — it's the rate you actually walk away with."

**"Can I try one load before committing?"**
> "Absolutely. No contracts, no commitment. Run one load with us and see the rate we get you. Our service agreement is month-to-month with 30 days notice either way."

**"That's too expensive for my volume"**
> "Let's look at actual numbers. If you're hauling [X] loads/week at [Y] CPM, our fee is $[Z]/week. Would you like me to show you what our carriers typically earn after fees?"

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Carrier pushes back hard on rate | Offer 30-day trial at reduced rate (5%); full rate after |
| Carrier tries to renegotiate after signing | Review at 90-day mark if performance warrants |
| Competitor undercuts significantly | Analyze: is competitor sustainable? Offer value-add (advance capability, faster payment) |

# SKILL LL — Carrier Retention & Churn Prevention
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "LL-carrier-retention-churn"
name: "Carrier Retention & Churn Prevention"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 18
priority: high
trigger: "Weekly automated churn risk scan for all active carriers. Also triggered by specific early-warning events."
inputs:
  - carrier_id: "string"
  - behavioral_signals: "from TMS — acceptance rate, contact frequency, complaints"
  - performance_data: "from 25-carrier-performance-scoring"
outputs:
  - churn_risk_score: "float 0.0–1.0 (1.0 = imminent departure)"
  - risk_factors: "array of identified warning signals"
  - intervention_playbook: "specific actions to take for this carrier"
  - outcome: "retained | churned | at_risk"
integrations:
  - TMS/CRM
  - WhatsApp (outreach)
  - Email
depends_on: ["25-carrier-performance-scoring"]
triggers_next: []
tags: [retention, churn, carrier-success, relationship, early-warning]
---

## Purpose

Detect when a carrier is considering leaving before they actually leave. Intervene with the right action at the right time. Losing a carrier costs 6–12 weeks of replacement recruiting and onboarding, plus lost revenue during the gap.

## Churn Risk Signals

### Behavioral Warning Signals (Weighted)

```python
CHURN_SIGNALS = {
    # High-weight signals (strong predictors)
    "load_acceptance_rate_drop": {
        "weight": 0.25,
        "trigger": "acceptance_rate < prev_4wk_avg * 0.75",
        "description": "Carrier rejecting 25%+ more loads than usual"
    },
    "response_time_increase": {
        "weight": 0.20,
        "trigger": "avg_response_time > prev_avg * 2",
        "description": "Taking much longer to respond to load offers"
    },
    "complaint_submitted": {
        "weight": 0.20,
        "trigger": "any_complaint_last_14_days",
        "description": "Explicit complaint = high churn signal"
    },
    
    # Medium-weight signals
    "revenue_decline": {
        "weight": 0.15,
        "trigger": "weekly_revenue < prev_4wk_avg * 0.80",
        "description": "Earnings dropped 20%+ from their baseline"
    },
    "check_call_compliance_drop": {
        "weight": 0.10,
        "trigger": "check_call_rate < 0.80",
        "description": "Becoming less communicative — disengagement signal"
    },
    
    # Lower-weight signals
    "asked_about_competitors": {
        "weight": 0.10,
        "trigger": "mentioned_competitor_in_conversation",
        "description": "Explicitly asked about other dispatch services"
    }
}

def calculate_churn_risk(carrier_id: str) -> float:
    carrier = get_carrier(carrier_id)
    total_score = 0.0
    
    for signal_name, config in CHURN_SIGNALS.items():
        if evaluate_signal(carrier, config['trigger']):
            total_score += config['weight']
    
    return min(1.0, total_score)
```

### Risk Tiers

| Score | Tier | Action | Timeline |
|-------|------|--------|---------|
| 0.0–0.2 | STABLE | Routine engagement | Weekly report |
| 0.3–0.4 | WATCH | Proactive check-in | Within 48 hrs |
| 0.5–0.6 | AT_RISK | Personal call from dispatcher | Within 24 hrs |
| 0.7–0.8 | HIGH_RISK | Intervention + incentive offer | Within 4 hours |
| 0.9–1.0 | CRITICAL | Emergency retention call | Immediately |

## Intervention Playbooks

### Playbook 1: Revenue Drop (Most Common Cause)

If carrier's earnings have dropped:
```
Call carrier:
"Hey [Name], I pulled your numbers for the past few weeks and I noticed your 
earnings are down from where you were. I want to make sure that's not something 
we're doing wrong on our end. Are you finding the rates not good enough? 
Are the lanes not working for you?"

Listen. Then:
- If rate issue: commit to target rate improvement for next 2 weeks
- If lane issue: update carrier profile preferences immediately
- If market issue: explain current market conditions + outlook
- If personal issue: express understanding, ask what would help
```

### Playbook 2: Acceptance Rate Drop

If carrier is rejecting 40%+ of load offers:
1. Review last 10 rejected loads — what was the pattern?
2. Were rates below floor? Adjust search parameters.
3. Were timings wrong? Update availability schedule.
4. Was it the lanes? Update preferred destinations.
5. Call carrier: "I noticed you've passed on several loads. Help me understand what you're looking for so I can stop sending you the wrong stuff."

### Playbook 3: Complaint Received

Within 2 hours of any complaint:
1. Acknowledge immediately: "I hear you and I'm looking into this right now."
2. Investigate: what actually happened? Is the complaint valid?
3. If valid: apologize, explain how it won't happen again, offer credit on next invoice
4. If not valid: explain calmly with data, but acknowledge their frustration
5. Follow up in 7 days: "I wanted to check in after last week..."

### Playbook 4: Competitor Mention

If carrier mentions another dispatch service:
```
"I appreciate you being upfront about that. Can you tell me what they're 
offering? I'm not going to badmouth them, but if there's a real gap between 
what we're doing and what you need, I'd rather fix it than lose you."

After learning the competitor offer:
- If price: "We can match/beat that if you commit to [X] loads/week"
- If feature: "We can add that — what specifically would help you?"
- If personality: "Let me connect you with [other dispatcher] who might be a better fit"
```

### Playbook 5: Silent Disengagement (Response Time Increasing)

Send personal WhatsApp message:
```
"Hey [Name], I just wanted to check in personally. I've noticed we haven't 
connected as much recently and wanted to make sure everything is going well. 
Is there anything we could be doing better for you? Your success is important 
to me and I want to make sure we're still the right fit."
```

## Weekly Churn Report (Every Monday)

```
CARRIER RETENTION REPORT — Week of March 16–22, 2026

STABLE: 42 carriers | WATCH: 5 carriers | AT_RISK: 2 carriers | CRITICAL: 1 carrier

AT RISK:
• Johnson Freight (MC-112233): Acceptance rate dropped from 82% → 51% last 2 weeks.
  Revenue -22% vs 4-week avg. TRIGGER: Earnings dropped + reduced engagement.
  ACTION: Dispatcher call today. Review lane preferences.

• Martinez Transport (MC-445566): Check-call compliance 61% last 3 weeks.
  Mentioned "might go with someone else" on 3/18 call.
  ACTION: Personal call from owner-level today. Competitor mention detected.

CRITICAL:
• Davis Trucking (MC-778899): No response to 4 load offers in 72 hours.
  Last load delivered 12 days ago with no new assignment accepted.
  ACTION: Emergency retention call within 2 hours. Prepare incentive offer.

CHURNED LAST 30 DAYS: 2 carriers (reason: relocated to FL — not preventable)
```

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Carrier leaves despite intervention | Document reason; improve playbook; replace in pipeline |
| False positive (carrier fine but signaled as risk) | Tune signal weights; note in model |
| Carrier won't respond to any outreach | Mark CHURNED after 14 days no contact |
| Competitor offer is objectively better | Honest discussion: "I can't match that today, but here's what we're working on" |

# SKILL MM — Shipper Direct Outreach
================================================================================

---
skill_id: "MM-shipper-direct-outreach"
name: "Shipper Direct Outreach"
version: "1.0.0"
phase: 0
priority: medium
trigger: "Weekly automated campaign. Also triggered when carrier has reliable lane history in a specific corridor."
inputs:
  - target_shipper_type: "enum: manufacturer | distributor | retailer | 3pl"
  - target_corridor: "region or specific lane"
  - carrier_capacity: "available equipment + lanes"
outputs:
  - shipper_leads: "array of qualified shippers contacted"
  - direct_booking_agreements: "any shippers who agreed to direct terms"
  - crm_updates: "shipper prospect pipeline updated"
integrations:
  - LinkedIn Sales Navigator API
  - Apollo.io / ZoomInfo (shipper contact data)
  - Email (SendGrid)
  - CRM
depends_on: []
triggers_next: ["HH-dedicated-lane-management"]
tags: [shipper-direct, direct-booking, lead-generation, bypass-broker, outreach]
---

## Purpose

Build direct relationships with shippers, bypassing freight brokers entirely. Direct freight eliminates the broker's 15–25% margin, giving carriers higher rates or the dispatch service better economics on negotiated spreads. Industry leaders like Convoy and Echo started this way.

## Why Direct Freight Matters

| Metric | Broker Load | Direct Shipper |
|--------|------------|---------------|
| Rate vs market | At market | 8–15% above market |
| Relationship stability | Zero — load board | Long-term, predictable |
| Load quality | Variable | Known commodity, known facility |
| Dispatch effort | High (negotiate every load) | Low (auto-schedule) |
| Dispatcher margin | 6% of broker rate | 6% of higher direct rate |

## Target Shipper Identification

### Ideal Direct Shipper Profile

- Ships 10–50 loads/week (not too big to need dedicated carrier, not too small to matter)
- Has consistent lanes (same origin → destination repeatedly)
- Is currently using spot market or small brokers (indicates frustration)
- Located in carrier's operating corridor

### Data Sources for Shipper Prospecting

1. **Internal TMS history**: Which shippers appear repeatedly on BOLs? These already trust the carrier's performance.
2. **DAT Lane Analysis**: What lanes does the carrier run most? Who ships those lanes?
3. **LinkedIn Sales Navigator**: Search "Director of Logistics" / "Transportation Manager" in target metro areas
4. **FreightWaves / Industry Publications**: Announcements of new distribution centers
5. **Facility geo-data**: Any industrial parks near where carriers regularly deliver

## Execution Steps

### Step 1 — Mine Internal Data for Warm Leads

```python
async def find_shipper_leads_from_history(carrier_id: str):
    """Find shippers that appear repeatedly on our carrier's BOLs."""
    
    # Query completed loads for recurring shipper/receiver names
    recurring_shippers = await db.query("""
        SELECT 
            shipper_name,
            shipper_address,
            COUNT(*) as load_count,
            AVG(agreed_rate_cpm) as avg_cpm,
            array_agg(DISTINCT destination_city) as destinations
        FROM loads
        WHERE carrier_id = %s 
          AND status = 'CLOSED'
          AND pickup_date > NOW() - INTERVAL '6 months'
        GROUP BY shipper_name, shipper_address
        HAVING COUNT(*) >= 3  -- Shipped with us 3+ times
        ORDER BY load_count DESC
    """, [carrier_id])
    
    return recurring_shippers
```

### Step 2 — Outreach Sequence

**Email 1 (Day 1) — Introduction:**
```
Subject: Direct freight relationship — [Carrier Name] serving your [Origin → Destination] lane

Hi [Name],

[Carrier Company] has been reliably serving the [Origin City → Destination City] lane for the 
past [X] months, most recently hauling for [Broker Name] on your behalf. We've delivered 
[X] loads to your facility with a 97% on-time record.

I'm reaching out because we're building direct relationships with shippers on this lane — 
which means better communication, a dedicated driver who knows your facility, and 
rates that work for both of us (without the broker in the middle).

Would you have 15 minutes this week to discuss what a direct arrangement might look like?

[Name] | [Title] | CortexBot Dispatch
```

**Email 2 (Day 5) — Value Proof:**
```
Subject: Re: Direct freight — [Carrier Name] performance data

Following up with some data that might be relevant:

In the past 6 months on your lane:
- On-time delivery: 97.2%
- Zero cargo claims
- Average response time for capacity confirmation: 22 minutes
- [X] loads hauled, [X,XXX] miles completed

For context, the average DAT spot market rate on your lane is $X.XX/mile. 
Direct carriers on dedicated agreements typically run at $X.XX/mile — 
the difference is reliability and planning certainty on your side.

Happy to share more or jump on a quick call.
```

**Email 3 (Day 12) — Simple Ask:**
```
Subject: One question — [Carrier Name]

Hi [Name],

Last touch from me — if direct freight isn't something you're considering right now, 
no problem at all. We'll continue serving your freight through the broker network 
with the same reliability.

If there's ever a time you want to discuss it, my contact info is below.

Best,
[Name]
```

### Step 3 — Discovery Call (If Shipper Responds)

Questions to ask:
1. "How many loads/week are you typically moving on [Origin → Destination]?"
2. "Are you currently using a TMS, or routing through a broker?"
3. "What are your biggest frustrations with the current arrangement?"
4. "What does your typical freight look like — commodity, weight, trailer type?"
5. "Do you have consistent day-of-week patterns, or is it variable?"

Goal: Understand if a dedicated lane agreement (Skill HH) makes sense.

### Step 4 — Direct Rate Proposal

If shipper is interested:
```
DIRECT FREIGHT PROPOSAL
Carrier: [Carrier Company] | MC#: [X]

Lane: [Origin] → [Destination]
Equipment: 53' Dry Van / Reefer
Proposed Rate: $X.XX/mile all-in
Detention: 2 hrs free, $50/hr after
Volume Commitment: Minimum [X] loads/week
Contract Term: 6 months renewable
Payment Terms: Net 15

Benefits vs Broker:
• Direct communication — no middleman
• Consistent driver, knows your facility
• Flexible scheduling
• 15-minute confirmation turnaround
```

### Step 5 — CRM Tracking

```json
{
  "shipper_id": "SHIP-001",
  "company": "Acme Manufacturing",
  "contact": "John Smith — Director of Transportation",
  "email": "jsmith@acme.com",
  "phone": "+15551234567",
  "lanes_of_interest": ["Nashville TN → Atlanta GA"],
  "loads_per_week_estimate": 5,
  "current_broker": "Echo Global",
  "outreach_status": "EMAIL_2_SENT",
  "lead_source": "internal_bol_history",
  "load_count_with_us": 12,
  "last_contact": "2026-03-20",
  "notes": "Frustrated with broker communication delays per email response"
}
```

## Error Handling

| Situation | Action |
|-----------|--------|
| Shipper says broker contract prevents direct | Note; re-engage in 6 months when contract may expire |
| Shipper interested but rate too high | Negotiate; remember: any rate above broker load = win |
| Shipper ghosts after initial interest | One more touch in 30 days; then quarterly nurture |
